pretty much all that there is.<br />(a surprising number of major composers are represented - only Richard Strauss' two works for piano-left hand and orchestra are missing).<br />Finally, after years of therapy, he was able to use both hands in a 2009 CD of three Mozart piano concertos.<br /><br />CDs 1, 2 and 4 are mono recordings, 1954-1956.<br />CDs 3 and 5-19 are stereo LP recordings, 1956-1963.<br />The &#34;original jackets&#34; for CDs 3, 6, 8 and 9 indicate that they are mono, but the CDs are stereo. *<br />The left-handed works on CDs 20-22 were recorded 1991-1993.<br />The Mozart concertos on CD 23 were recorded in 2008.<br />Since CDs 20-23 were never released on LP, there are no program notes on the back of their &#34;original jackets&#34;.<br /><br />Approximately half the material is new to CD - especially welcome is the Brahms Quintet with the Julliard Quartet (CD 18).<br />Aside from the new material, I don't think anything was newly remastered.<br />I did an A-B comparison of several of them with their previous CD incarnations, and could detect no difference.<br />Timings are absolutely identical, which is not what you would expect if Sony went back to the analog master tapes.<br />Quite good sound, nonetheless.<br /><br />WARNING: This is a LIMITED EDITION (like the Horowitz). 1781162646|4.0|Joyland is not a horror novel. It's not really a ghost story. It has a ghost story in it, and that's about it. And the horror is all in the humanity.<br /><br />Joyland is really a novel about a young man, a 21 year old named Devin Jones, who has taken up a job at Joyland, an amusement park in Heaven's Bay, North Carolina. it is about a boy who's first real love has just left him for another man, leaving Devin (Dev to most, Jonesy to some, Kiddo to others) a virgin; heart broken. He decides to take a semester off of college and stay on at Joyland during the autumn. After he saves a little girl from choking on a hotdog, his boss agrees.<br /><br />There is a ghost (supposedly) haunting the Horror House, a ghost that supposedly roams the tracks of the funhouse ride after her throat was slit and her body was dumped. Devin's friend, Tom, saw the ghost, and Devin and Tom's girlfriend, Erin decide they will investigate the murder.<br /><br />But really, the mystery and horror of Horror House take a back seat to the heart-felt story of Devin's relationship with Annie and Mike Ross. Mike is condemned to a wheelchair and will die soon (he's got Muscular Dystrophy), and his mother knows it. In fact, it's why everyone in town believes her to be a cold-hearted woman. But Devin breaks through to her after he helps her son fly his kite--her son who has a psychic ability.<br /><br />If you are looking for suspense, this may not be the novel for you. If you are looking for horror, go find a copy of IT, or THE SHINING. Joyland is a different novel from King. It is somewhere between 11/22/63 and The Body. A coming of age story that satisfies and has the reader sitting back reminiscing about his/her own early twenties. That is the joy of reading King, and that Joyland certainly delivers a great, dramatic story with just a twinge of mystery and a twist of King's love of the supernatural.<br /><br />Very highly recommended!

B00BTHWFBK|4.0|After decades of waiting, 3/4's of the original Black Sabbath (including Ozzy) reunite for what has to be one of the most anticipated CD's of the year, the boomtastic \\"13.\\" I can testify that it was worth the wait. Producer Rick Rubin told the band to go back to their early albums to get a feel for what he was expecting to produce, and the band took it to heart. This is metal so dense, it cuts like used crankshaft motor oil. It's that heavy.<br /><br />If you're looking for speedy riff rocking, it's not here. This is the sound that created such anthemic dirges as \\"War Pigs\\" or \\"Sweet Leaf.\\" There's even a touch of Ozzy the blasphemer as he raises the question \\"Is God Dead?\\" And they pound that riff into submission for over 8 minutes. Granted, Ozzy's voice is showing its weathering, but Tony Iommi and Geezer Butler still have the magic spooky touch. (Audioslave drummer Brad Wilk fills in for Bill Ward.) \\"End Of The Beginning\\" snakes a demented blues riff to kick the album off with a oozing pounce. Or there's \\"Dear Father,\\" which tackles the subject of abuse.<br /><br />The band has never been scared of heavier topics, which \\"Dear Father\\" and the anxiety provoking \\"Methademic\\" show. (Given Ozzy's recent trip to rehab, maybe even closer to home than known.) The band even throws a few touchstones from the old days in when \\"Zeitgeist\\" pays homage to \\"Planet Caravan.\\" Even with that obvious reference, \\"13\\" pounds and stomps like the monsters Black Sabbath were at the peak of their powers. The sense of dread and thrill of doom still permeate the best of the songs here, and - despite their age - the band doesn't sound like they are pandering to their past or trying to stay current. \\"13\\" is every bit as tasty as \\"The Devil You Know\\" (by Heaven and Hell with Dio), just down tuned and packed with 50% more evil.<br /><br />Worth the wait and better than anyone could have possibly expected at this point in their collective life, \\"13\\" is a triumphant comeback. \\"I Ain't no hero to come and save you,\\" Ozzy wails in \\"Peace of Mind.\\" Well, actually guys, you are. Thanks for saving heavy metal for 2013.come and save you,\\" Ozzy wails in \\"Peace of Mind.\\" Well, actually guys, you are. Thanks for saving heavy metal for 2013.
